< review>
These local coffee shops are so much better than something like Starbucks.  Great service here with a lot of open space, although the interior space could have more comfortable seating.  I shared the single outside picnic table with another patron, which was great for the perfect weather.  The honey latte with cinnamon was excellent, as was the prosciutto and gruyere croissant (on a weekday).  Unfortunately,  I tried the same order on a Saturday shortly after they opened,  and the croissant was a cold ball of dough,  meat and cheese inside.   It seemed right out of the fridge that day.  Yuck.  The person I brought with me that time had the same thing and agreed completely.  I'll still give 4 stars to cut them a break given my first experience.<//review>

<pics>None< /pics><rating>5<//rating><Review>They rotate through different roasters, but it doesn't matter whom they are featuring, Ambrose consistently has the best cup of coffee in Pasadena. Their prices are great too, <$3 for their dialed-in drip. They pay their baristas a fair, no-tipping wage too.

If you're a regular, don't get attached to a specific seat. They reorganize their large open space constantly. (I think it depends on whatever artist they are featuring, but I don't know that for sure.) The music is sometimes a little raucous for the early morning for my taste, but that's true at every coffee shop I frequent.

Overall, Ambrose is Pasadena's best-kept coffee shop secret. I hope the word gets out.< /Review><UserId.>116379308468239799674</UserId.><name>Elijah Davidson<//name><response>{'time': 1563403838058, 'text': 'Thanks for this amazing and detailed review!'}<//response><Time>1559582793421</Time></record></dataset><record>

<Rate>5</Rate><text>I'll admit I was a little chary about the charcoal latte hype but I was pleasantly surprised by the Ambrosia latte here. It cost $5 and was a good blend of deep espresso flavor mellowed out by the nuanced highlights of rose and charcoal. The iced version was a little creamier while the hot version was slightly more complex -- I think the warmth allows them to develop on your palate more.

A few other things: service was extremely friendly and despite the cafe having just the one barista, we got our drinks relatively quickly. Alternative milks including Oatly are free, which is a really lovely perk. There was plenty of space to sit inside and out, although the cafe is co-joined up against a larger space.</text>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>

<review>I love sushi - a mixture of Japanese and Korean food. A mixture of hit and miss.

The restaurant has an ambience of typical American diner more than Asian Restaurant. Spacious, clean and relax ambient.

Service is attentive, fast and courteous

Complimentary Miso soup is promptly served as soon as we sat down. Warm a bit watered down, bland.
Had Golden California roll, crunchy on the outside just a bit tad thick on rice with filling of mayo-dressed crab sticks with bits of avocado-cucumber; am not sure i tasted mango in it.

The shrimp tempura is crispy but dry that it becomes too crumbly to touch. Shrimp is too small to be be noticeably tasty. Tempura sauce is also watered down-bland.

The only saving grace is the hot-stoned beef bibimbap. Served sizzling hot that made rice crispy at the bottom, the way I liked my hot bibimbap. Generous serving of fresh-crisp vegetables and beef strips that are tender and tastily marinated. The only letdown was the topped egg that is already fried very well done. But it's one good bibimbap, one of my comfort food.< /review><Pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOAC4xdHQVjJkoqOHyDb22hVvah8PMXq3nWW47H=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipP2izl8H8t_haQwlsvuWxlkWd8PMM9_4oAR2ngl=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pictures>< resp>

< Text>
Came here for lunch for the first time with my co-worker. Parking lot closest to the restaurant was starting to fill up. When we came in, we were acknowledged with a friendly unison of "Hajimemashite" from the staff and servers. We were seated immediately, looked through the menu, & were served free appetizers (edamame, two sushi slices and cucumber). The sushi slices were actually surprising to be honest because I have never dined at a Japanese restaurant that included sushi samples as the appetizers.

My co-worker ordered a bento box & I ordered a Chicken Dupbap. My co-worker didn't finish her bento, but she commented on its deliciousness. The Chicken Dupbap had this grilled flavor to it as well as chili tomato sauce, but it wasn't spicy & lacked salt. It was filling overall.

The atmosphere was calm & the interior was kind of strange. Korean, Japanese, & American? It's great that it's catered to different cultures. However, it's quite interesting how the menu had Korean & Japanese food; yet the atmosphere was modern American. Service was pretty quick, but that's only because we dined shortly after the restaurant opened at 11:30 AM. Servers were quick on their feet, attentive, & direct. I didn't get to taste their sushi, but next time I will. The Korean dishes were tasty, despite lack of salt. I will definitely return a second time &  recommend this place to my friends.</Text>

<username>Kenneth Ikemiya<//username>< Text>
This is a restaurant I've visited for almost 25 years, admitting a few years between meals. We've had some good meals over the years, but this last visit didn't meet my expectations. First of all, prices have gotten absurd. $52 for a dish of seafood pasta is ridiculous. It was pretty tasty, but the portions are miniscule, almost to the point of feeling like I needed to guard my plate from "tasters" at my table. My kids wolfed down their adult meals and were browsing for more. The wait staff seemed like they had recently graduated from bus boy status, so the meal flow was awkward. My dish I felt was the best of the pastas, and it fell off quickly after that. Where did Cassandra's go that I loved years ago?<//Text>

<rating>5< /rating>< text>
Must haves: Spinach gnocchi Au gratin and seafood fettuccine.  Thinking about those two dishes now makes my mouth water. The gnocchi is fluffy and goes perfectly with the melted cheese and cream sauce. Even though it was piping hot, I couldn't help but keep eating it and willing to burn my tongue a bit. As for the seafood fettuccine - I'm a big fan (and very picky) of lobster pastas with some sort of white sauce. I wish this one had a bit more lobster and less mussels so the seafood taste could infuse into the sauce more. However, this was still impeccable. I loved the not too creamy sauce that coated the fettuccine perfectly.

The desserts were good but nothing to die for.

Only downside to this restaurant was the price. The seafood fettuccine was $33 and you only get half a lobster, 2 shrimps and some clams and mussels.

I'd still go back for the gnocchi though!</text>

< review>
Beautiful restaurant with a cozy setting and outdoor patio. The croque madame I ordered wasn't bad, a bit too rich, and with the fries a bit too large a portion. This is a matter of preference for me, though, since French restaurants should typically run smaller portions if they want to be authentic. The fresh bread and olive tapenade was delicious, however. The thing that annoyed me the most is that their business description on Google reads "... with an outdoor patio once frequented by Van Gogh". This is of course very incorrect, and comes from the fact that they purchased a dining table, once used by Van Gogh, as a museum piece.<//review>

<Review>We loved this place the first two times we were there, but tonight's experience has ruined our favorable opinion of them

Most places call their customers if there is going to be an issue with their reservation. This place doesn't feel the need to bother with that courtesy. They're so small they are probably confident that someone will fill the empty spot.

We made reservations for 7:15, but upon arrival were told that we would be sitting outside under the overhang. There are two such tables like that. The rest are inside and the other outdoor tables have no protection from the weather.

We made it known that this wasn't ideal because it was raining, to which she replied in a very condescending tone that it would be a very long wait for a table inside. In an even more irritating and smug tone she said she could provide a blanket if that would be too cold for us.

Restaurant people, please note that customers almost always expect a table inside especially if it's cold and/or rainy outside. Sitting outside is almost never a pleasant surprise. As we scrambled to find another restaurant on OpenTable we noticed that even the Hog's Breath Inn knows to not make reservations for outdoor seating.

Trying to find an open spot at another restaurant at the last minute is almost impossible. All the decent ones are already packed by that time.

We'll never be back, but I'm sure they're not worried. There will be plenty of other potential customers attracted to their gimmick of a house that's been converted to a restaurant. It wears old after a while though.< /Review><Pictures>None<//Pictures><resp>None< /resp>< GmapID>

<Date>1515100149984< /Date>< Review>
We have been coming to this restaurant for the past 10 years. We know the prices are steep and the food is pretty good but it held some sentimental value for us as a family. Sadly we will not be returning as customers. My mom has been struggling with stage four cancer for a couple of years now and we decided to come up for a memorable vacation not knowing if it will be the last. Long story short the experience we had at Casanova was very disappointing. From the moment we got there our waiter was rude and could not answer very simple questions like drink pricing and wine recommendations. Nor did he try and find the answers he seemed bothered by the questions rather than helpful. The carbonara my mother in law ordered was mediocre at best. The dish my parents and I ordered was pretty good (we all had the fettuccini). But when it was time to get our bill we all paid with separate forms of payment which the waiter told us to do since he didn‚Äôt want to separate checks. The waiter ‚Äúaccidentally‚Äù charged $160 to me twice and managing staff could not return the money because they had to get a hold of the owner. They said they voided both charges but $320 was taken from our account or held. my mother in law was charged with the total bill which was $253. Told us to come back next day to get it resolved. By this point almost $600 is tied up at this one restaurant. 2 days later still unresolved and not put back in our account. Go to Demetra‚Äôs better portions better staff, better food.</Review>

<Text>This was out best dining experience this trip in Carmel. First of all, the ambience is very nice. The seats are scattered around the restaurant in small quarters under a roof or outdoors on their open patio with heat lamps, giving every table privacy - usually only a few tables around your own. The service was nice. Out waitress Rachel was not too familiar with ingredients to satisfy our wish to eat eggless vegetarian, so she got someone from management who helped us out. The restaurant seeks to give a small town European flair & it is successful in that. The decorations are also nice. The food was simply outstanding. We had grilled artichoke, but not with the aioli which had egg, but marinated with garlic & butter, & this was simply the best artichoke dish we had. The garlic added a nice flavor. I usually avoid gnocchi, but the spinach gnocchi literally melted in my mouth & was heavenly. We also ordered french fries but simply could not eat that. We will be sure to come back.< /Text>< date>
1350084027690</date>

Last night very upset with Casanova,  my parents went to dinner here for 20 years, my father passed away, so I thought Mom would enjoy eating at their favorite restaurant.  I made reservations 2 days ahead for table for two.  Arrived on time and we were shown to a table for 6 with 3 people already having dinner.  This was to be a special dinner for us, and we were expected to share a meal with strangers.  When we inquired to see if there was a mistake, we were told due to the rain adjustments had to be made.  This ruined our whole evening, and we decided to leave. A manager came out the door after us and offered us a table outside, my mother replied,"we reserved an inside table".  Very disgusted with this restaurant, actually shocked that they would offer an outside table to an 88 year old woman on a cold, damp rainy day. I am a black and white person and what Casanova did was just plain wrong, sad for you!</text>

<date>1532559022647< /date><rating>3<//rating><Text>I've been here 3 times. Each time the expierence is about the same. 3 stars.
Pros
1) Cute setting, looks small from the outside but it's actually really big with lots of little rooms and even a downstairs.
2) Food is fresh

Cons
The food isn't that memorable. Recently I has osso bucco that was very tender and just lightly flavored which was really good. What kept it from great is that it wasn't hot. I think it wasn't reheated fully.

(The gnocchi appetizer is delicious and may be the only memorable dish I've had out of my 3 visits.)

Salad is drenched in dressing (it has been this way all 3 times we've been, we always forget it'll be like that until it arrives). The parm on it is delicious if you can taste it without dressing.

Scallops were just ok. They were cooked perfectly but the avocado mousse was not a good combo with the scallops, strawberries and the trout eggs. I felt like the flavors clashed.

It is known for being a romantic restaurant but that highly depends on where you sit. If say only a small amount of tables would be romantic, the rest are either in a busy walkway and/or in the loud, and draftier larger rooms. Its cute but not romantic.

They put tip amounts on the bill if you want to pay 20% 25% or 30% tip which is really obnoxious! Who pays 30% tip, especially for just an okay experience.

The staff is nice of course, but they're so busy and not always on it as they should be. Took a couple times to order our drinks, didn't supply a drink menu, then I had asked for a lime in my drink and it was forgotten the second round. Not big deal but who tips 20%+ for that?

Then a different person than our server came to close out our bill, as I was looking at it she came over and gave me a new receipt and said it had the bottle of water on it, it was forgotten on the first receipt she gave me. It was awkward and felt rushed. And if you forget a $6 bottle of water that is way overpriced anyways just let it go.

All in all, I'm not impressed.

7D, Tree House and Anton & Michel are all better food/date night options each with their own different style.< /Text>< Pictures>

<text>Let me preface what I'm about to say with "We love dogs!" BUT...
We were celebrating a birthday, and looking forward to a nice meal in Carmel. We arrived on time for a reservation this evening. There were several parties in the outside seating area, all of which seemed to have large dogs accompanying them for dinner. A scuffle broke out between three of the animals; people began pulling their animals apart to avoid a bristled mess. Not a very pleasant entrance for such a touted restaurant. It didn't end there...We entered the building to be met with a woman who barley acknowledged us. She was busy talking to another patron about, you guessed it, his dog. We patiently waited, she fluttered off while another young woman asked if she could help. Yes, thank you. We told her the reservation time, and she seemed genuinely dazed, then said, "You'll need to wait for Christian, she'll seat you." We stepped back awkwardly while a large party of 15 arrived. They sat them while we waited. Funny, another couple came in and this same young woman asked if she could help them. They advised of a reservation, she then responded, "You'll need to wait for Christian." Not quite sure what her roll was in this establishment, but clearly she should not be asking if she could be of any help. The flutterer came back mumbling at the no-help gal "...and we need to take care of Lexor, his dog..."
We did eventually get seated in a couple of uncomfortable wicker chairs and stared at each other. We decided $30 for a ravioli dinner at this restaurant just wasn't worth it. We shrugged, got up and began walking the canine gauntlet. What a hoot. It was PC comical. So many other restaurants that will engage their patrons upon arrival, seat them quickly, and at the very least, treat them better than the dogs. Here's a helpful hint: designate a corner of the restaurant AWAY from your main entrance for dogs, and hint #2: remember, it's the human animal that pays your bills.< /text></record></dataset><record>

<user>111428638507422761457<//user>< username>
Paul Vasquez</username>
<Date>1366511758353< /Date><rate>5</rate>< review>
My wife and I took a trip to the Monterey/Carmel region, and this was the highlight for us. The decor is very old-European; the service was excellent; and the food was good enough to make a second trip to Carmel worth the journey.

For starters, they give everyone a sun-dried tomato tapenade with cheesy cracker sticks. The tapenade is actually good enough to eat with a spoon, which we did because we didn't' want to miss a bit of it. At first, I thought perhaps it was made from roasted tomatoes, but the waitress said it was a mixture of sun-dried tomatoes, olives, and parmesan cheese. At any rate, it was fantastic.

For our entrees, we were in the mood for Italian, so I ordered the spinach gnocchi, and my wife ordered the Linguine Scampi. Both were excellent. The gnocchi sauce was very rich and cheesy. The scamp was also in a cream sauce with heavy basil seasoning, which colored the sauce green. We shared both dishes, and both were excellent as well.

Finally, we wanted to give the restaurant a full vetting, so we decided to order a dessert and share it. We ordered a lemon tart with raspberry sorbet. Again, it was well worth the money, definitely something you would have to come here to get.

In sum, we would definitely make the trip to try the rest of the menu, and I'd recommend it to a friend looking for an upscale Italian or French dining experience.<//review>
